Page 1 of 7
PAKISTAN
SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
STAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
Public Health Administration. Project Organization & Ioplenentation
1.        After an introductory paragraph on the federal structure, this annex
focuses on the structure of the provincial level public health organization and
on how the proposed project supported sub-programs and their implementation
arrangements at the provincial level relate to it.
Public Health Administration
Federal Level
2.        The Ministry of Health (MOH), in association with the Ministry of
Planning and Development and Ministry of Finance, is responsible for health
policy-making.  With the exception of the provision of health services for
government employees and containment of communicable diseases (such as malaria),
KOH is =  responsible for providing health services directly.  It coordinates
health service provision through the provincial Health Departments and
independent autonomous bodies such as the National Institute of Health.1
Organization charts for the health services at federal and provincial levels are
presented in Charts LA, 1B and lC.  The federal government retains overall
responsibility for the coordination and orderly management and development of all
health services. The main work of the MOH is carried out through the Minister,
Secretary and Director General of Health to whom report a range of deputy
director generals, deputy secretaries and project directors.
Provincial Level
3.        Provincial Departments of Health have responsibility for providing
health services. The provincial Secretary formulates health policy, exercises
final control over the budget and has direct control over teaching hospitals and
special institutions. The provincial Director General of Health Services (DHS)
is responsible for preventive and curative services; all District Health Officers
(DHO) and Superintendents of District Hospitals report to him as do all
provincial heads of 'priority programs' and vertical programs, e.g. imuunization,
basic health services, maternal and child health headed by the Inspectress of
Health Services,  and malaria control.   Lack of coordination between the
Secretariat and the Directorate often hinders smooth implementation. Significant
decisions relating to districts, e.g., appointment of middle level and senior
I/ Other fedoral governant organisations which provide basic health services include the armed forces,
Ministry of the Interior, Ministry of Kasbhir Affairs and Northern Areas and various public enterprises.



- 109 -
Annex 6
Page 2 of 7
staff and budget allocations, are made at the provincial level. Organizational
arrangements differ somewhat between provinces as shown by Charts lB and 1C.
District Level
4.        District services include (a) a district health office headed by a DHO
reporting to the DHS; (b) a District Headquarters Hospital, headed by a Medical
Superintendent also reporting directly to the DHS; (c) tehsil hospitals, Rural
Health Centres, Basic Health Units, dispensaries, and Maternal and Child Health
Centres reporting to the DHO; (d) local management of vertical programs reporting
on technical matters to the respective provincial heads of each program, e.g.
immunization and malaria control and to the DHO on administrative matters;
(e) municipal health services (including environmental sanitation) controlled by
municipal authorities; and (f) population welfare, through a District Population
Welfare Officer, who is at the same level as the DHO but reports to the
provincial Secretary/Director General Population. Thus, there are minimally four
district level officers, who have to coordinate the provision of health services.
In the larger towns and cities, a major part of the establishment, maintenance
and management of hospitals and health centers, and environmental health and
sanitation are assigned to municipal committees and corporations; a few of these
operate sizeable systems. (Proposals have been made to establish District Health
Boards in each district. While their exact functions have yet to be decided, it
is likely that they will be advisory and include representatives of the Health
Department and of other departments and authorities concerned, together with
representatives of other interested organizations including NGOs.)
5.        DHOs have responsibility for overall health matters in their district.
However, in practice, DHOs lack the authority needed to appoint, dispose and
discipline staff; manage budgets and authorize repairs; and plan and coordinate
the activities of their districts.   Moreover, their social status compares
unfavorably with those of District Hospital Superintendents, creating serious
disincentives for preventive versus curative medical work (staff are
interchangeable between these posts).
Pro.ram and Proiect Organization
6.        The proposed program and integrated project organization includes the
establishment of:
(a) Program Steering Committees, which will be chaired by the provincial
Secretary of Health and include the Secretary of Population Welfare, Director
General of Health Services, senior representatives of Finance, Planning &
Development, Communications and Works, senior DOH staff and representatives of
cooperating local bodies such as universities, medical colleges, municipalities



- 110 -
Annix 6
Page 3 of 7
and NGOs2.   The Project Directors will be the member/secretary and the
Committees will meet initially at least every three months; attendance is
expected to be at most around twelve to facilitate decision taking;
(b) Technical Committees, chaired by the Directors General of Health Services.
These committees will capitalize on the knowledge of the specialists, inside and
outside government but at a lower level than in the Steering Committee, to
resolve rapidly operational problems that arise. The Technical Committees will
meet monthly during the early stages of implementation and less frequently
thereafter;
(c) Additional resources to strengthen the implementation capacity of the
provincial Departments of Health; and
(d) Provincial Health Development Centres (see below).
Program and Project Implementation
7.        The proposed project is part of the provincial development program and
will be implemented by the existing organization and structure of the two
provincial Departments of Health. The priority sub-programs supported by the
project will be implemented through the provincial Departments of Health and
within those Departments the Deputy Directorates for (a) Basic Health Services,3
and (b) Communicable Disease Control (malaria, health education etc); the
Inspectorate of Health Services; and the Provincial and District Health
Development Centres. The Lahore Metropolitan Corporation and the Bahawalpur,
Sarghoda and Quetta Municipal Corporations (MCs) will implement the urban health
subcomponent of the project through their existing medical departments in the
MCs.  Additionally, Lahore MC will establish a small coordinating body to
facilitate progress.   The NGOs concerned will implement their subcomponents
through their existing structures. All Project activities will be facilitated
by strengthened management and implementation capacity. The additional resources
will especially assist with preparation of project documentation (program and
financial), obtaining the necessary Government approvals and monitoring
compliance with donor agreements, reviewing progress, and facilitating the start
of new activities.   The Punjab has established a special directorate to
coordinate external assistance and Balochistan is expected to make similar
arrangements. The directorates include a Director and Deputy Director of FHII.
Overall guidance for the project will be through the Program Steering Committee
supplemented by the Technical Committees (see Project Organization); a diagram
summarizing these links is at Chart 2.
VJ Representation would vary a little between provinces: for xoxmple, in the Punjab, senior representatives
from the Lahore Metropolitan Corporation will attend, while in Balochistan the Lady Dufferin Hospital (an
MM) will be represented.
jV In the Punjab, there is a Director for Basic Health Services: the position equivalent to the Deputy
Director in other provinces is entitled Director in the Punjab. Throughout thic report, when reference is
made to a Deputy Director, the relevant official in the Punjsb is a Director.

Anex 6
Page 4 of 7
8.        The Deputy Director for Basic Health Services and the Inspectress of
Health Services will be mainly responsible for implementing the sub-programs for
the first comDonent (Strengthening of Primary Health Services) within their
respective areas of responsibility. The Deputy Director for Communicable Disease
Control and other Deputy Directors concerned together with the head of the
medical department of each MC and the designated officers of the NCOs concerned
will be also involved in implementing this component. The Project Director will
be responsible for coordinating the timely delivery of project inputs, for
assisting with their effective integration into the package of services provided
at public health facilities, and for facilitating coordination with the Deputy
Directors responsible for hospitals and other Deputy Directors and equivalents
concerned. At the District level, one of the existing Assistant District Health
Officers will be responsible for coordinating project activities under the
overall guidance of the District Health Officer.
9.        For the second component (Staff Development), the implementation of the
upgrading and expansion of the female paramedical schools will be through the
regular DOH channels and therefore be mainly the responsibility of the
Inspectress of Health Services, the professional heads of discipline and senior
tutors of the institutions  concerned.    For activities  such as curricula
development and tutor training, the existing heads of discipline and Deputy
Director concerned will take the lead. Coordination of their work will be helped
by a small cross-discipline advisory group which will include representatives of
each of the main female cadres, of the Provincial Health Development Centre (see
below), and chaired by a representative from the Directorate of Health Services.
In Balochistan, the special efforts to be made for improving female staff
recruitment and retention will be led by two small teams of additional staff,
working under the direction of the Inspectress of Health Services and the
Director General.   The Project Director will facilitate all of the above
activities.
10.       The in-service training of the second component and the Management
Development component, the third component, will be mainly implemented through
the Provincial Health Development Centres and the District Development Centres.
Provincial Health DeveloRment Centre (PHDC)
11.       The PHDCs, one in Quetta and one in Lahore, will be responsible for
facilitating the implementation of the provincial level aspects of the management
development program, the human resources development programs, the health an
nutrition education program, and the supporting research and monitoring
activities. The Director of the PHDC will report to the Director General of
Health Services. Where suitable Government staff already exist, e.g. technical
trainers, they will be transferred into the PHDC; the remainder will be recruited
and trained. Substantial technical assistance has been included to support the
PHDC, especially in the early project years.   The Project Director will be
responsible for coordinating the timely delivery of project inputs to the PHDC
and for facilitating PHDC activities and their coordination with other on-going
provincial activities.



- 112 -
Ann- 6
Page 5 of 7
12.       The PHDCs (see Chart A) will comprise four units:
(a) The Management Development Unit will be responsible for supporting
provincial planning and relating it to management systems, management
information  systems,   logistics,  communication,   financing,  and
designing and implementing provincial level management training. It
will also assist with district level management and supervisory
training.
(b) The Staff Development Unit will be responsible for in-service training
development, both technical and non-technical aspects. It will assist
with assessing training needs, design and develop course packages and
modules, train trainers at divisional and district levels, and conduct
some provincial level courses.
(c) The Health and Nutrition Education Unit will develop and provide in-
service training to health professionals in communication skills.
Training for these tasks will be an integral part of most in-service
technical training courses rather than separate courses. The program
will also include: assistance for and coordination of the work of the
district health/nutrition educators; developing prototype health
education materials; and coordination with other related education
activities such as those of the Department of Population Welfare.
(d) The Research and Monitoring Unit will promote field studies (mainly
through contracts), coordinate monitoring activities and systems and
facilitate operational research.
The proposed staffing is:
Management Development Unit:
1    program director/planner (Director of overall PHDC)
1    public health doctor/PHC management trainer
1    hospital administration trainer
Staff Development Unit:
1    program director/in-service training planner
4    in-service trainers
Health and Nutrition Education Unit:
1    program director/health and nutrition educator
1    health and nutrition education planners/trainers
1    media research/design officers (in the Punjab there will be 2)
3    media specialists/technicians

Punjab)

General PHDC Support Staff

8    other support staff
District Health Development Centre (DHDC)
13.       At the district level, the above activities will be implemented through
DHDCs located in each district headquarters town of the Punjab. In Balochistan,
due to the small size of the districts and fewer numbers of health staff and
facilities, there will be one DHDC in each division headquarters town*. Each
DHDC will: (a) serve as a facility for training health staff, particularly mid-
level female personnel; (b) be a district health and nutrition education center;
(c) be a district health staff meeting center; (d) be a center for holding
workshops, seminars and training community leaders; (e) conduct small scale
studies; and (f) be a library and resource center. These Centres will be headed
by a senior medical officer supported by one health/nutrition education officer,
and 3-5 other training staff (including 2-3 LHV trainers and 1-2 multipurpose
paramedical trainers, with the addition in the Punjab of a monitoring/research/
evaluation officer). The staff officers of the District Health Office and the
District Headquarters Hospital will be resource persons for the DHDC. The head
of the DHDC will report to the District Health Officer on administrative matters,
as do all district staff, and to the PHDC on technical matters. The DHDC will
provide key assistance to the District Health Officer in orientating and
supporting the district health management teams.   The Project Director will
facilitate the establishment of the DHDCs either through the PHDC or the district
line management as appropriate.   The introduction of the DHDCs will follow the
same phasing as that of their respective districts. Chart B shows the structure
of a DHDC.
Construction Arranjements
14.       The provincial Departments of Communications and Works (C&W) will be
responsible for the civil works aspects of the project including site surveys,
line plans, working drawings,  tender documents and site supervision.   New
3. Reformose to the district level should be read as applying to the division levl in Ualochistn.

construction in the project comprises: (a) medium sized facilities consisting
of public health schools in Chakwal and Sahiwal (Punjab), one hostel at each of
four existing female paramedical schools in Lahore and Multan (Punjab) and in
Quetta and Khuzdar (Balochistan), NGO maternity hospitals and schools in the
Punjab (2) and Quetta (1), an NGO public health school in Islamabad, and a public
health laboratory in Quetta (varying from US$100,000-US$700,000 equivalent per
institution); (b) two PHDCs and about 35 DHDCs which are modest in scale and
geographically dispersed (varying from US$100,000-US$250,000 equivalent); and
(c) 14 new MCH Centers (under US$25,000 equivalent). Standardized design for
all DOH facilities in both provinces will be used to the extent possible since
concepts are simple, functional and well adapted to local conditions.
Renovations/extensions to existing buildings include rehabilitation of two
government maternity hospitals, one in Balochistan (to be run by an NGO) and one
in the Punjab, extensions to female paramedical schools in Balochistan (2) and
the Punjab (2), and upgrading of about 220 existing MCH Centres and dispensaries
to include labor rooms and accommodation for LHVs. Most of the extensions are
small (under US$100,000 equivalent) while the bulk of renovation fall under a
much lower cost threshold (under US$20,000 equivalent).

- 145 -
Annex 8
PAKISTAII
SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
STAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
Procurement Procedures
For items to be financed from the Credit, the standard bidding
procedures of the Government are considered appropriate, provided that the
following are observed:
(a)   Prospective bidders should be allowed at least 30 days to submit
bids from the date of the invitation to bid or availability of bid
documents, whichever is later, and require the bid invitation to
so specify;
(b)   Require the invitation to bid to be advertiz-d in the local
newspapers;
(c)   Require contracts to be awarded to the bidder who submits the
lowest evaluated responsive bid in accordance with the criteria
set out in the bid documents. To this end, the bid documents may,
where appropriate, specify factors, in addition to price, which
would be taken into account in determining the lowst evaluated
bid, and how such factors would be quantified or otherwise
evaluated;
(d)   Require the bids to be opened in public so that the bidders, or
their representatives are present at the bid opening, and require
the invitation to bid to so specify;
(e)   Preclude negotiations to be carried out with the lowest, or any
bidder, except with the Association's concurrence;
(f)   Require the time of the bid opening to be the same as that
specified for the latest delivery of bids;
(g)   Require late bids to be rejected; and
(h)   Require contracts expected to run more than 12 months to contain
suitable provision for any necsesary adjustments in materials and
labor costs.

Annex 11
Page 1 of 2
PAKISTAN
SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
STAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
Proiect Sunervision
1.    IDA's Resident Mission in Pakistan will  monitor program and project
progress throughout, particularly concentrating on the more detailed aspects of
project implementation.
2.    Formal program and project supervision vill be based on regular six-monthly
review missions.
3.    In about March of each year,  there will be a joint review by the
cooperating donors (IDA, German KFW and British ODA) and the federal and
provincial governments as appropriate.  This Annual Review will, inter alia,
assess program and project progress, propose solutions to identified problems,
agree on a work plan for the coming fiscal year, and agree on the recurrent and
development funds required for both the program and project for the coming fiscal
year.
4.    In about September of each year, there will be a Technical Review mission
which will focus mainly on substantive technical issues of project
implementation. Typically these would include issues arising in aroas such as
maternal and child health care, family planning, paramedical staff training, and
management and institutional development. KFW and ODA representatives would join
these missions as necessary.
5.    Before the arrival of each mission in Pakistan, tho Departments of Hoalth
would circulate a six-monthly progress report which would focus on outstanding
issues in addition to being a concise progress rocord. Missions would take up
disbursement and procurement matters as necessary.
6.    During the first supervision mission, a Droiect launch workshoD will be
organized.  Tho workshop will ensure that all officials concerned are fully
familiar with the details of the project and, additionally, will help the
executing agencies to: (a) produce a detailed work plan for the first year of
implementation; (b) better undorstand IDA and co-operating donor procurement,
disbursement and other procedures; and (c) review plans for monitoring and
evaluation.
7.    A mid-term review, carried out in the third year, will evaluate thoroughly
the program and project, assess to vhat extent objectives are being met, identify
changes needed to improve effectiveness, and modify as necessary the project
design and detailed content.
8.    A supervision plan is given bolow.
